  PIPELINE FLOW:
    1. Complexity estimation → determines workflow budget
    2. Scaffold LLM call → generates project skeleton (workflows, deps, arguments)
    3. Per-workflow detail LLM calls → generates steps, variables for each workflow (parallel, 3 concurrent)
    4. Spec merge → combines scaffold + all workflow details
    5. Spec validation → checks activity catalog compliance
    6. XAML compilation → converts spec to .xaml files via tree assembler + XAML generator
    7. Quality gate → validates expressions, types, namespaces, structure
    8. Meta-validation → secondary review pass
    9. Remediation → auto-fixes where possible
    10. Packaging → builds .nupkg archive
    11. DHG generation → creates Developer Handoff Guide

--- SDD CONTENT (input to LLM) ---
"## 1. Automation Architecture Overview

### 1.1 Architecture choice (RPA vs Agent vs Hybrid)
This process is best delivered as a **Hybrid automation (Deterministic integration + GenAI content generation)**:
- **Deterministic steps** (calendar read, contact lookup, send email, duplicate prevention, logging) are stable, auditable, and should be implemented as standard unattended workflows orchestrated by **Orchestrator**.
- **Non-deterministic step** (writing a “warm, funny, sarcastic” message in your voice) is best implemented using **UiPath GenAI Activities**. We will treat the generated text as “suggested content” and apply validation/guardrails before sending.

We will **not** use a fully agentic orchestration as the primary control plane, because:
- The process is time-based, short-running, and rules-driven (calendar “Birthdays”, Personal>Home email rule, “do nothing if no email found”).
- Operational predictability (retries, idempotency, run history, audit) is stronger in Orchestrator + Data Service than in an agent-only loop.

### 1.2 Execution model and topology
- **Execution type**: **Unattended only** (tenant has 12 unattended slots; requirement is fully autonomous; no Assistant).
- **Runtime**: Cloud Orchestrator-managed background execution. No UI automation is required; we favor **Integration Service activities** for resiliency.
- **Triggering**: Orchestrator **time-based trigger** daily at **08:00** in a configured timezone asset.

### 1.3 UiPath services used and why
- **Orchestrator**: scheduling, job execution, retries, assets, logs, alerts (via Monitoring), process versioning.
- **Integration Service**:
  - **Gmail connector** (mandatory) to send emails via connection **“ninemush@gmail.com”**.
  - **UiPath GenAI Activities** via connection **“prajwal.shambhu@uipath.com”** to generate the message (native UiPath; no OpenAI).
- **UiPath GSuite/Google activities**: read Google Calendar “Birthdays”. (Calendar connector is not listed as an active Integration Service connection, so calendar read will be done with UiPath Google activities that use OAuth/connection in Studio/Orchestrator assets.)
- **Data Service**: persistence for run history, event idempotency (“already sent today”), and traceability (who, when, email chosen, subject hash).
- **Storage Buckets**: store prompt templates, “voice style” grounding snippets (optional), and per-run artifacts (sanitized) such as the final rendered email body for audit/rollback.
- **Test Manager**: regression suite (calendar edge cases, multiple birthdays, missing emails, GenAI failure, Gmail throttling).
- **Action Center / Maestro / Agents / DU / Comms Mining / AI Center**: available but **not in the critical path** for v1 because the requirement is “fully autonomous” and the process does not ingest documents or triage inbound messages. We will still design optional hooks (disabled by default) for future governance and review.

### 1.4 Operability and SLA story
- **SLA**: Greetings sent within **5 minutes** of 08:00 trigger for all birthdays that have an email in Contacts.
- **Monitoring**:
  - Orchestrator job success/failure and duration thresholds (alert if job fails or exceeds 10 minutes).
  - Data Service “SendStatus=Failed” records trigger operational alert email to **ninemush@gmail.com** (sent via Gmail connector) with run id and error summary.
- **Idempotency**:
  - Prevent duplicates by persisting a per-person/per-date key in Data Service (and optionally Gmail message-id in record).

---

## 2. Process Components and Workflow Breakdown

### 2.1 High-level workflow decomposition
We will implement as a **single unattended Orchestrator process** with internal modular workflows (Invoke Workflow File) following **REFramework-lite** principles (init/process/end, retries, consistent logging) but not full queue-driven REFramework since daily volume is low.

**New Orchestrator Process Name (unique):**
- `BirthdayGreetingsAutonomousV4_HybridGenAI`

**Workflows**
1. `Main.xaml`
   - Orchestrator entrypoint.
   - Reads config/assets.
   - Calls calendar fetch, loops through events, processes each person, writes Data Service status.
2. `WF_InitConfig.xaml`
   - Loads Orchestrator assets (timezone, calendar name, prompt template path, subject template, max retries, etc.).
   - Validates Integration Service connections available (Gmail, GenAI).
3. `WF_GetTodaysBirthdayEvents.xaml`
   - Reads Google Calendar **“Birthdays”** for today (start/end timestamps in configured timezone).
   - Returns list of events with fields: `EventId`, `EventTitle` (full name), `EventDate`.
4. `WF_ProcessBirthdayEvent.xaml`
   - Input: name, eventId, date
   - Steps:
     - Check Data Service if already processed/sent for this event+date → skip.
     - Find email in Google Contacts by name:
       - select **Personal** first, else **Home**, else **Not Found**.
     - If no email found → **do nothing** (per final requirement).
     - Generate greeting via GenAI with guardrails.
     - Validate output (length, no placeholders, no unsafe content, no links if disallowed).
     - Send email via Gmail connector `ninemush@gmail.com`.
     - Persist outcome in Data Service.
5. `WF_GenAI_GenerateMessage.xaml`
   - Encapsulates prompt construction and GenAI call.
   - Keeps any sensitive prompt context out of logs (log only a hash/length).
6. `WF_SendGmail.xaml`
   - Encapsulates Gmail send activity and standardizes error mapping.
7. `WF_ErrorHandler.xaml`
   - Standard error logging + screenshot capture (even though mostly integration-based, we capture a screenshot of the robot session as best practice).
   - Writes failure record to Data Service and optionally emails operations alert to ninemush@gmail.com.

### 2.2 Trigger and schedule
- **Time trigger**: Daily 08:00 (timezone from asset, default e.g., `America/New_York`).
- **Concurrency**: single job instance (avoid double-run). If Orchestrator allows, set “Prevent overlapping runs”.

### 2.3 Human-in-the-loop (Action Center) stance
Baseline is **fully autonomous**; therefore **no Action Center user tasks are created** in the normal path.

However, to make the solution production-operable, we will implement an **optional “Review Mode” feature flag** (Orchestrator asset `Enable_ActionCenter_Review` default `False`). When enabled, messages that fail validation can be routed for review.

**Action Center Task Catalog (optional, disabled by default):**
- Catalog: `BirthdayGreeting_Review`
- Form Schema (if enabled):
  - `RunId` (string, read-only)
  - `EventId` (string, read-only)
  - `BirthdayDate` (date, read-only)
  - `RecipientName` (string, read-only)
  - `DetectedEmailPersonal` (string, read-only)
  - `DetectedEmailHome` (string, read-only)
  - `SelectedEmail` (string, editable, required; regex email validation)
  - `Subject` (string, editable, required; max 120)
  - `Body` (multiline string, editable, required; min 20, max 2000)
  - `Decision` (choice: `ApproveAndSend`, `RejectDoNothing`; required)
  - `ReviewerComment` (string, optional)
- SLA Configuration:
  - Due in: `2 hours`
  - Warning at: `1 hour`
  - Escalation: email to `ninemush@gmail.com` if overdue (sent by automation via Gmail connector)
- Data persistence:
  - Task references Data Service entity `BirthdayGreetingAttempt` (see Section 8).

### 2.4 Use of Maestro
Not required for v1: there is no multi-stage case management or parallel human+system orchestration. Orchestrator trigger + a single job is sufficient and simpler to operate.
Future: if you add approvals, drafts, photos, or multi-step personalization, Maestro can orchestrate a “Birthday Greeting Case” with gateways and SLAs.

### 2.5 Reuse of existing processes
Existing deployed processes include multiple “BirthdayGreetingsAutonomous…” variants. To avoid naming conflicts and unintended coupling:
- We will **not** call those as sub-processes unless their XAML is confirmed reusable and version-controlled.
- We will implement `V4` cleanly but can reuse proven prompt patterns/activities from `BirthdayGreetingsAutonomousV3GenAI` if source is available.

## 5. Exception Handling Strategy

### 5.1 Exception taxonomy
**Business exceptions (handled, continue)**
- No birthdays today → end successfully.
- Contact email not found (no Personal/Home) → do nothing for that person; continue loop.
- Duplicate detected in Data Service (already sent today for same event/person) → skip.

**System exceptions (retry/abort depending on scope)**
- Google Calendar read failures (auth, transient 5xx).
- Contacts lookup failures.
- GenAI transient errors/timeouts.
- Gmail send throttling or auth failures.

### 5.2 Retry strategy
- Per integration call: **2 retries** with exponential backoff (e.g., 5s, 15s) for transient faults.
- Per person processing: if GenAI fails after retries, mark attempt as `Failed_GenAI` and continue to next person (so one failure doesn’t block other greetings).
- Whole job: Orchestrator job retry policy can be enabled (1 retry) but must be paired with Data Service idempotency to avoid duplicate sends.

### 5.3 Screenshot-on-error
Even though the solution is integration-first, we still implement:
- In every top-level `Try/Catch`, capture a screenshot and attach path/reference in logs.
- Store screenshot artifacts in a Storage Bucket folder: `/runs/<RunId>/error/`.

### 5.4 Dead-letter handling
Not queue-driven; instead:
- Write failed attempts to Data Service with `Status=Failed` and `ErrorCategory`.
- A secondary scheduled job (optional) `BirthdayGreetingsAutonomousV4_FailureNotifier` can scan failures and email a summary to ninemush@gmail.com (still fully autonomous).

---

## 6. Security Considerations

### 6.1 Credential and secret management
- Use **Integration Service connections** for Gmail and GenAI (tokens managed by UiPath).
- For Google Calendar/Contacts OAuth (if using GSuite activities), store secrets in **Orchestrator Assets** (Credential assets) and restrict visibility.

### 6.2 RBAC
- Orchestrator folder roles:
  - Robots: execute permissions only.
  - Developers: edit packages and assets.
  - Business owner: view logs, view Data Service entities (read-only).
- Data Service permissions:
  - Only the automation service account can write entities; human users read-only unless review mode enabled.

### 6.3 Data handling / privacy
- Do not log full email body by default; log:
  - message length, hash, and “validation passed/failed”.
- Store PII minimally in Data Service:
  - recipient name, selected email (needed to send/audit).
- Storage Bucket artifacts are optional; if enabled, retain max 30 days.

---

## 7. Test Strategy

### 7.1 Test levels
- **Unit tests (Studio)**:
  - Name parsing, label selection logic (Personal > Home), dedupe key generation, prompt builder.
- **Integration tests**:
  - Calendar read for “Birthdays” with known test events.
  - Contacts lookup for known contacts with both labels.
  - Gmail send to a controlled test recipient.
  - GenAI response validation with deterministic constraints.
- **End-to-end tests**:
  - “No birthdays” day.
  - “Multiple birthdays” day.
  - “Missing email” scenario (must do nothing).
  - “Already sent” scenario.

### 7.2 Test Manager usage
- Create a **Test Project**: `BirthdayGreetingsAutonomousV4_Tests`
- Define test cases mapped to requirements and execute regression before each deployment.
- Schedule nightly regression (optional) against a sandbox calendar.

---

## 7a. Governance Compliance

Automation Ops is not enabled; therefore governance policies cannot be centrally enforced here. We will still align to standard governance practices:
- Naming conventions: `BGN_V4_<Component>` for workflows/assets.
- Mandatory error handling: Try/Catch around each integration boundary, consistent logging, screenshot-on-error.
- No hard-coded credentials or emails (except calendar name “Birthdays” which is configurable by asset).

## 8. Data Model and Entity Design (Data Service)

### 8.1 Entity: `BirthdayRun`
Purpose: one record per Orchestrator job run.

Fields:
- `RunId` (Text, required, unique) — Orchestrator Job Key
- `TriggerTime` (DateTime)
- `TimeZone` (Text)
- `CalendarName` (Text) default “Birthdays”
- `BirthdaysFoundCount` (Number)
- `ProcessedCount` (Number)
- `SentCount` (Number)
- `SkippedNoEmailCount` (Number)
- `FailedCount` (Number)
- `Status` (Choice: `Started`, `Completed`, `CompletedWithFailures`, `Failed`)
- `StartedAt` (DateTime)
- `EndedAt` (DateTime)
- `ErrorSummary` (Text, optional)

### 8.2 Entity: `BirthdayGreetingAttempt`
Purpose: one record per birthday person per date (idempotency + audit).

Fields:
- `AttemptId` (Text, required, unique) — recommended: hash of `EventId + BirthdayDate`
- `RunId` (Text, relationship to `BirthdayRun.RunId`)
- `BirthdayDate` (Date)
- `CalendarEventId` (Text)
- `RecipientFullName` (Text)
- `SelectedEmail` (Text, nullable)
- `EmailLabelSelected` (Choice: `Personal`, `Home`, `None`)
- `GenAIModelConnection` (Text) default `prajwal.shambhu@uipath.com`
- `Subject` (Text)
- `BodyHash` (Text) — SHA-like hash (store hash not full body by default)
- `BodyLength` (Number)
- `SendStatus` (Choice: `NotAttempted`, `Skipped_NoEmail`, `Sent`, `Failed_GenAI`, `Failed_Send`, `Failed_Other`)
- `SentAt` (DateTime, nullable)
- `GmailMessageId` (Text, nullable)
- `ErrorCategory` (Text, nullable)
- `ErrorMessage` (Text, nullable)
- `RetryCount` (Number)

### 8.3 Relationships
- `BirthdayRun (1) -> (many) BirthdayGreetingAttempt` via `RunId`.

### 8.4 How workflows use entities
- `Main.xaml` creates `BirthdayRun` at start, updates at end.
- `WF_ProcessBirthdayEvent.xaml`:
  - checks `BirthdayGreetingAttempt` by `AttemptId` to prevent duplicates,
  - writes status transitions and timestamps.

---

## 8. Agent Architecture (mandatory for hybrid automation)

Even though we are not using an agent as the control plane, we will define a **minimal autonomous agent** for the GenAI drafting step to centralize prompt/guardrails and allow future evolution (e.g., adding “style memory”, holiday variants). This keeps “AI behavior” separately governed from the deterministic workflow.

### 8.1 Agent Type
- **Autonomous agent** (tool-using, but invoked by the Orchestrator process; not conversational)

### 8.2 Agent Identity
- **Name**: `BirthdayGreetingWriterAgent`
- **Purpose**: Generate a short birthday email body in the user’s warm, funny, sarcastic voice using only provided context.
- **Behavioral system prompt (high level)**:
  - “Write a personal birthday email message in a warm, funny, sarcastic tone. Keep it friendly and non-offensive. Do not include sensitive topics. Do not hallucinate facts. Use only the recipient name and that today is their birthday. Output plain text only.”

--- PDD CONTENT (input to LLM) ---
"## 1. Executive Summary

The “birthday greeting new” project automates a daily routine where, at approximately 8:00 AM, birthdays are checked from a dedicated Google Calendar (“Birthdays”) and a personalized birthday email is sent from the user’s Gmail account. The current process is fully manual and is occasionally missed due to forgetfulness. The proposed solution is a fully autonomous, unattended UiPath automation scheduled via Orchestrator Triggers. It will retrieve today’s birthday events from the “Birthdays” calendar, determine the correct recipient email address from Google Contacts (preferring **Personal** over **Home** when multiple addresses exist), generate a warm/funny/sarcastic message in the user’s voice using **UiPath GenAI Activities** (native UiPath capability; no OpenAI), and send the email using the **Gmail connector (Integration Service) with connection “ninemush@gmail.com.”** If no birthdays exist, the automation ends with no further action. If no email is found for a birthday contact, the automation will skip sending and take no action (per final requirement).

## 2. Process Scope

This PDD covers the end-to-end process for daily birthday greeting emails triggered at 8:00 AM and executed autonomously in the UiPath cloud environment using unattended robots. The process begins when the scheduled trigger runs and queries the Google Calendar named “Birthdays” for events occurring “today.” For each identified birthday, the process attempts to find an email address in Google Contacts for the person’s full name. When multiple email addresses are available, the automation selects **Personal** first, then **Home**. When a usable email is available, the process generates a personalized birthday greeting in the user’s specified voice (warm, funny, sarcastic) and sends it from **ninemush@gmail.com**.  

Out of scope for this iteration are: use of Google Drive, use of OpenAI/Azure OpenAI directly, use of Slack/Teams/Twilio channels, and use of Google Photos or image attachments. Relationship metadata is also out of scope because the calendar events contain only full name (no relationship field).

## 3. As-Is Process Description

![As-Is Process Map](/api/ideas/17c6186d-d425-4c1e-bc15-6ac71394c906/process-map/image?viewType=as-is&v=1774761019590)

The current (“As-Is”) process is initiated by the user at 8:00 AM as a self-reminder to send birthday greetings (Step 1.0). The user opens Google Calendar and navigates to the dedicated calendar “Birthdays” (Step 2.0), then checks the day’s events to see whether any birthdays occur today (Step 3.0). The user makes a decision based on the calendar view: if there are no birthdays, the process ends with no action (Step 4.0 → Step 5.0).  

If there is a birthday today, the user selects the birthday person by full name (Step 4.0 → Step 4.1). The user then determines the recipient’s email address (Step 6.0). In practice, the email is in Google Contacts; however, the user often relies on Gmail behavior as well—when typing the person’s name in the “To” field, Gmail autocomplete commonly suggests the address based on prior correspondence. The user decides whether an email address is available (Step 7.0). If an email is found, the user drafts a personal birthday message in their own voice (Step 8.0) and sends it via Gmail (Step 9.0), ending the process once sent (Step 10.0). If no email is available, the user skips sending and ends the process without a greeting being sent (Step 7.0 → Step 7.1 → Step 7.2).

## 4. To-Be Process Description

![To-Be Process Map](/api/ideas/17c6186d-d425-4c1e-bc15-6ac71394c906/process-map/image?viewType=to-be&v=1774761019590)

The proposed (“To-Be”) process is a fully autonomous unattended automation scheduled daily at 8:00 AM and orchestrated through UiPath Orchestrator. The automation type is best implemented as a **Hybrid** of deterministic RPA/integration automation plus native GenAI generation (agent-like content generation), with no human-in-the-loop required for the baseline flow.

The workflow begins when an Orchestrator time-based trigger initiates the job at 8:00 AM (To‑Be Step 1.0). The automation retrieves today’s birthday events from the Google Calendar named “Birthdays” using a UiPath Google Calendar activity (Step 2.0). The workflow evaluates whether any birthday events exist for the current date (Step 3.0). If none exist, the process ends immediately with no notifications and no “forgotten” scenario (Step 3.0 → Step 4.0).

If birthdays exist, the automation iterates through each birthday person returned for the day (Step 4.1). For each person, it looks up email addresses from Google Contacts (Step 5.0). The selection rule is explicit: if multiple addresses are returned, choose **Personal** first; if Personal is not available, choose **Home**; if neither exists, treat as not found (per SME approval). The automation then checks whether a usable email is available (Step 6.0). If no email is found, the automation skips that person and proceeds to the next birthday record without sending any notification email or draft (Step 6.0 → Step 6.1 → Step 6.2).

If an email is available, the automation generates a personalized birthday message in the user’s warm, funny, sarcastic voice using **UiPath GenAI Activities** (Step 7.0). The prompt will be grounded on the available structured details from the calendar event (primarily the full name and the fact it is their birthday today). A lightweight validation step checks whether the generated message is usable (Step 8.0). In this iteration, the intended future state is to proceed autonomously when the message passes basic safety/format validation, and then send the email from Gmail via Integration Service using the connection **“ninemush@gmail.com”** (Step 10.0).  

The To‑Be map includes optional human review via Action Center (Steps 9.0–9.1) if the message is flagged as needing review, but given the requirement for fully autonomous execution, the baseline configuration will set conservative prompt constraints and validation rules so that the “Needs Review” branch is minimized or disabled unless required by compliance. After sending, the workflow marks the person as completed (using Data Service for traceability and avoidance of duplicates) and continues until all birthday people have been processed, then ends (remaining loop steps in the To‑Be map).

## 5. Pain Points and Inefficiencies

The principal operational pain point is missed execution: the user sometimes forgets to check the calendar and send greetings at 8:00 AM. Even when remembered, the current process requires repeated manual actions—opening the calendar, confirming birthdays, searching for the person’s email (either through Gmail autocomplete or Google Contacts), drafting a bespoke message, and sending it. This manual drafting step is time-consuming and inconsistent in quality depending on the user’s availability and context. Additionally, the manual process does not create a reliable audit trail of what was sent and to whom, and it does not handle multiple birthdays in a structured, repeatable way.

## 6. Automation Opportunity Assessment

This process is a strong automation candidate because it has a predictable schedule, a clear data source (Google Calendar “Birthdays”), a repeatable set of actions (lookup contact, generate message, send email), and low exception complexity. The key “judgment” component—writing a personal message in the user’s voice—can be reliably supported by UiPath’s native GenAI capabilities while keeping orchestration, logging, and delivery deterministic through UiPath Orchestrator and Integration Service.

Recommended automation type is **Hybrid (RPA + GenAI)**: integration-driven retrieval of calendar events and sending via Gmail connector, combined with GenAI-driven drafting for personalization. The automation will run on unattended robots (12 available) with Orchestrator scheduling and centralized monitoring. Data Service can be used to store run history and “already sent” markers to prevent duplicates and improve resiliency (e.g., if a job retries).

Platform alignment to constraints is direct: Gmail sending must use the Integration Service Gmail connection **“ninemush@gmail.com”**; OpenAI usage is explicitly excluded; Google Drive is explicitly excluded; and the process must remain fully autonomous.

## 7. Assumptions and Exceptions

Assumptions: The Google Calendar named “Birthdays” is accessible to the automation identity and contains one event per person per year (or recurring events) with the person’s full name in the event title or a consistent field that can be parsed. It is assumed that Google Contacts contains the recipient email addresses labeled as **Personal** and/or **Home**, and that names in the calendar reasonably match names in Contacts to enable lookup. It is also assumed the Gmail Integration Service connection **“ninemush@gmail.com”** is authorized and permitted to send external emails.

Exceptions and handling: If there are no birthdays today, the automation ends quietly with no notification. If a birthday person is found in the calendar but no email address is found in Contacts under Personal or Home, the automation does nothing for that person and continues to the next (final requirement). If multiple emails exist, the automation selects **Personal** first; if not present, then **Home**; otherwise it treats the contact as having no usable email. If message generation fails (e.g., GenAI service transient issue), the job will follow Orchestrator retry policies and log the failure; depending on configuration, it can skip the person after a bounded retry to ensure the overall run completes.

## 8. Data and System Requirements

The automation requires access to the following systems and data sources within UiPath:

Google Calendar: The workflow must read events from the Google Calendar named “Birthdays.” Retrieval must filter for “today” in the correct timezone and support multiple events in a single day. The calendar event data required is at minimum the event title (full name) and event date.

Google Contacts: The workflow must query Google Contacts to retrieve email addresses for the person identified in the calendar event. The data required includes email values and their labels. The selection logic must prioritize **Personal** over **Home**. If a Google Contacts connector is not currently provisioned in Integration Service, the implementation will require either (a) adding/authorizing an appropriate Google Contacts/People API connector connection in Integration Service, or (b) implementing the lookup via supported UiPath activities/API calls under approved credentials.

Gmail (Integration Service): Email delivery must be performed using the Gmail connector through Integration Service with the existing connection **“ninemush@gmail.com.”** The workflow must populate: recipient email, subject, and body (generated message), and optionally include a consistent signature if desired.

UiPath GenAI Activities (Integration Service): Message generation must use UiPath native GenAI Activities (connection available: **“prajwal.shambhu@uipath.com”**). Prompting must be designed to consistently produce a warm, funny, sarcastic message, and include guardrails to prevent inappropriate content. Generated content should be treated as transient runtime data unless explicitly logged.

UiPath Orchestrator: A time-based trigger must run daily at 8:00 AM. Orchestrator must manage unattended execution, retries, and logging. Assets should store configurable values (calendar name “Birthdays”, sender mailbox “ninemush@gmail.com”, subject templates, timezone, and prompt template).

UiPath Data Service (recommended): A structured entity should store daily run records and per-person completion status (e.g., event ID/date, person name, chosen email, send timestamp, status). This supports auditability, duplicate prevention, and operational reporting.

Constraints: The design explicitly avoids Google Drive, OpenAI/Azure OpenAI direct usage, and Slack/Teams/Twilio. Photos are deferred to a later iteration. The process must execute fully unattended with no dependency on UiPath Assistant or user interaction."

## 4. Process Context (from Pipeline)

### Idea Description

Automate birthday greetings to friends and family

### PDD Summary

## 1. Executive Summary

The “birthday greeting new” project automates a daily routine where, at approximately 8:00 AM, birthdays are checked from a dedicated Google Calendar (“Birthdays”) and a personalized birthday email is sent from the user’s Gmail account. The current process is fully manual and is occasionally missed due to forgetfulness. The proposed solution is a fully autonomous, unattended UiPath automation scheduled via Orchestrator Triggers. It will retrieve today’s birthday events from the “Birthdays” calendar, determine the correct recipient email address from Google Contacts (preferring **Personal** over **Home** when multiple addresses exist), generate a warm/funny/sarcastic message in the user’s voice using **UiPath GenAI Activities** (native UiPath capability; no OpenAI), and send the email using the **Gmail connector (Integration Service) with connection “ninemush@gmail.com.”** If no birthdays exist, the automation ends with no further action. If no email is found for a birthday contact, the automation will skip sending and take no action (per final requirement).

## 2. Process Scope

This PDD covers the end-to-end process for daily birthday greeting emails triggered at 8:00 AM and executed autonomously in the UiPath cloud environment using unattended robots. The process begins when the scheduled trigger runs and queries the Google Calendar named “Birthdays” for events occurring “today.” For each identified birthday, the process attempts to find an email address in Google Contacts for the person’s full name. When multiple email addresses are available, the automation selects **Personal** first, then **Home**. When a usable email is available, the process generates a personalized birthday greeting in the user’s specified voice (warm, funny, sarcastic) and sends it from **ninemush@gmail.com**.  

Out of scope for this iteration are: use of Google Drive, use of OpenAI/Azure OpenAI directly, use of Slack/Teams/Twilio channels, and use of Google Photos...

### SDD Summary

## 1. Automation Architecture Overview

### 1.1 Architecture choice (RPA vs Agent vs Hybrid)
This process is best delivered as a **Hybrid automation (Deterministic integration + GenAI content generation)**:
- **Deterministic steps** (calendar read, contact lookup, send email, duplicate prevention, logging) are stable, auditable, and should be implemented as standard unattended workflows orchestrated by **Orchestrator**.
- **Non-deterministic step** (writing a “warm, funny, sarcastic” message in your voice) is best implemented using **UiPath GenAI Activities**. We will treat the generated text as “suggested content” and apply validation/guardrails before sending.

We will **not** use a fully agentic orchestration as the primary control plane, because:
- The process is time-based, short-running, and rules-driven (calendar “Birthdays”, Personal>Home email rule, “do nothing if no email found”).
- Operational predictability (retries, idempotency, run history, audit) is stronger in Orchestrator + Data Service than in an agent-only loop.

### 1.2 Execution model and topology
- **Execution type**: **Unattended only** (tenant has 12 unattended slots; requirement is fully autonomous; no Assistant).
- **Runtime**: Cloud Orchestrator-managed background execution. No UI automation is required; we favor **Integration Service activities** for resiliency.
- **Triggering**: Orchestrator **time-based trigger** daily at **08:00** in a configured timezone asset.

### 1.3 UiPath services used and why
- **Orchestrator**: scheduling, job execution, retries, assets, logs, alerts (via Monitoring), process versioning.
- **Integration Service**:
  - **Gmail connector** (mandatory) to send emails via connection **“ninemush@gmail.com”**.
  - **UiPath GenAI Activities** via connection **“prajwal.shambhu@uipath.com”** to generate the message (native UiPath; no OpenAI).
- **UiPath GSuite/Google activities**: read Google Calendar “Birthdays”. (Calendar connector is not listed as an active Integrati...

**Automation Type:** hybrid
**Rationale:** Pulling birthdays and sending emails is deterministic and best done with RPA/API actions, but generating a “warm, funny, sarcastic” message in your voice is judgment-based natural language generation, best handled via GenAI/agent capabilities.
**Feasibility Complexity:** medium
**Effort Estimate:** 1-2 weeks

### Decision Points (Process Map Topology)

**Any Birthdays Today?**
  - [No] → End (No Birthdays Today)
  - [Yes] → For Each Birthday Person (Full Name)

**Email Available?**
  - [No] → Skip Person (No Email Found)
  - [Yes] → Generate Personalized Birthday Message (Your Voice)

**More Birthday People Remaining?**
  - [Yes] → Continue to Next Birthday Person
  - [No] → End (All Birthday Greetings Processed)

  - [No] → End (All Birthday Greetings Processed)

--- SDD CONTENT (input to LLM) ---
"## 1. Automation Architecture Overview

### 1.1 Chosen automation type and rationale
This process is best delivered as **Hybrid (Deterministic RPA workflow + Native GenAI)**:
- **RPA (unattended)** is ideal for the deterministic steps: schedule at 8:00 AM in SME timezone, read Google Calendar events, look up Google Contacts emails, apply the “personal > home” rule, and send mail via Gmail connector. This must be **fully autonomous** and repeatable.
- **GenAI (UiPath-native)** is ideal for the non-deterministic step: generating a short message that matches the SME’s warm/funny/sarcastic voice with guardrails.

**We are not using a pure Agent-only design** because:
- Most steps are deterministic and have clear integration connectors; a workflow is more controllable, testable, and cheaper to operate.
- The tenant indicates **Agents availability with limited confidence**. We will use **GenAI Activities** as the primary message generator and treat “Agents” as an optional enhancement (see Section 8) without making the core solution depend on uncertain platform reachability.

**We are not using attended automation** because:
- Only unattended slots are available (11) and the SME requires fully autonomous execution.

### 1.2 Orchestration pattern
**Single-process scheduled unattended automation** (not dispatcher/performer, not queue fan-out) is optimal because:
- Daily volume is small (typically a handful of birthdays).
- There is no multi-transaction SLA requiring parallelism.
- A queue-driven model would add operational overhead (queues, retries, reconciliation) without meaningful benefit.

If volume grows materially (e.g., dozens+ per day across multiple calendars), we can evolve to **Dispatcher/Performer with Orchestrator Queues** for fan-out and parallel sends, but it is intentionally not the first design.

### 1.3 UiPath services used (and why)
- **Orchestrator**: schedule trigger at 08:00 SME timezone; process deployment; assets; logs; alerts (via job failures); robot allocation across 11 unattended slots.
- **Integration Service**: required integration mechanism (per constraint). We will use:
  - Gmail connector (existing connection **ninemush@gmail.com**, ID **0a0d5ee1-a1e8-477a-a943-58161e6f3272**)
  - Google Calendar connector (**new connection to be provisioned**)
  - Google Contacts/People connector (**new connection to be provisioned**)
- **UiPath GenAI Activities** (native): generate email body in SME voice; implement safety/tone guardrails; no OpenAI usage.
- **Data Service**: persist per-run/per-recipient audit (what was sent, to whom, when, status) and support idempotency (avoid duplicate sends in the same day if rerun).
- **Storage Buckets**: retain run artifacts (sanitized prompts/responses, error screenshots, and optional per-run JSON snapshots of event/contact resolution) for operability and troubleshooting.
- **Test Manager**: automated regression suite for date logic, email selection logic, and prompt/guardrail behavior using mocked datasets.

### 1.4 Why not Action Center / Maestro / Document Understanding / Communications Mining for this iteration
- **Action Center**: SME explicitly wants fully autonomous greetings and PDD defines silent skip conditions. Human-in-the-loop would reduce autonomy. We will still design an *optional* review path for “guardrail fail” (disabled by default).
- **Maestro**: BPMN/case management is unnecessary for a single scheduled automation with no required human tasks.
- **Document Understanding / Generative Extraction**: no documents in scope.
- **Communications Mining**: not needed; we are not triaging inbound email.

### 1.5 Deployment topology / runtime
- **Unattended execution** on existing 11 unattended slots.
- **Cloud-first** integrations via Integration Service connectors; no UI automation dependency required.
- **Licensing implications**: uses unattended robot runtime, Integration Service usage, GenAI Activities entitlement, and Data Service. No attended licenses required.

---

## 2. Process Components and Workflow Breakdown

### 2.1 New process and naming (avoid conflicts)
Existing deployed processes include `BirthdayGreetings Autonomous` and `BirthdayGreetingsAutonomousV2`.  
New fully deployed process name:
- **`BirthdayGreetingsAutonomousV3_GenAI`** (unique, non-conflicting)

### 2.2 Workflow structure (REFramework-inspired, not full REFramework overhead)
Given low complexity but the need for operability, we implement an **REFramework-lite** pattern:
- `Main.xaml` orchestrates Init → Get Data → Process Data → End with structured logging and centralized exception handling.
- Transaction item = one birthday event/person.

**Components**
1. **Init.xaml**
   - Read Orchestrator Assets (timezone, calendar name, subject template, tone instructions, guardrails thresholds).
   - Initialize Data Service context.
   - Initialize Storage Bucket folder path for the run (e.g., `runs/yyyy-mm-dd/jobId/`).

2. **GetBirthdays.xaml**
   - Use Integration Service **Google Calendar** to locate calendar ID for calendar name = `""Birthdays""`.
   - Retrieve events for “today” based on SME timezone.
   - Normalize event list into a typed list `BirthdayEvent`:
     - `EventId`, `EventStartDate`, `EventSummary`, `FullNameParsed`, `FirstName`, `RunDate`, `SourceCalendarId`
   - Deduplicate events (same name repeated) using `(RunDate, FullNameParsed)`.

3. **ProcessBirthdayEvent.xaml** (per event)
   - Resolve contact:
     - Use Integration Service **Google Contacts/People** search by `FullNameParsed`.
     - If 0 matches → **silent skip**, record “NoMatch”.
     - If >1 matches → **silent skip**, record “AmbiguousMatch”.
     - If exactly 1 match → extract emails and labels.
   - Select recipient email:
     - Prefer label = `personal`
     - Else label = `home`
     - Else none → **silent skip**, record “NoEmail”.
   - Idempotency check (Data Service):
     - If already sent for `(RunDate, RecipientEmail)` or `(RunDate, FullNameParsed)` with status “Sent” → skip to avoid duplicates on reruns.
   - Generate message:
     - Build prompt with FirstName and SME style asset.
     - Call **UiPath GenAI Activities** to generate body.
   - Guardrails validation:
     - Length limit (configurable) e.g., 60–120 words.
     - Must not include sensitive claims, money requests, threats, etc. (rule-based + GenAI self-check step).
     - Must not mention relationship (not stored).
     - If fails → default behavior in PDD is fully autonomous; we will **regenerate once** with stricter prompt. If still fails → **do not send** and record “GuardrailFail”.
   - Send email:
     - Use Integration Service **Gmail** (connection ninemush) to send.
     - Subject: `Happy Birthday, {FirstName}!` (selected option 1)
   - Persist audit:
     - Write to Data Service entity `BirthdayGreetingLog`.

4. **End.xaml**
   - Summarize results (counts: sent, skipped-no-email, skipped-no-match, skipped-ambiguous, guardrail-fail, errors).
   - Upload a run summary JSON to Storage Bucket.
   - If job failed: ensure screenshot + diagnostic bundle uploaded.

### 2.3 Execution type per component
- All workflows: **Unattended**
- GenAI generation: **Unattended** (via GenAI Activities)
- No attended steps.

### 2.4 Optional (disabled-by-default) human-in-the-loop design
Although not required by PDD, for safety we include a feature-flagged path:
- If `EnableHumanReview` (Orchestrator Asset) = True and guardrails fail twice → create Action Center task “Review Birthday Email Draft”.

Because PDD requests full autonomy, default is **False**.

**Action Center task definition (optional)**
- Task Catalog: `BirthdayGreetings_ReviewDraft`
- Form schema:
  - `RunDate` (Date, read-only)
  - `FullName` (String, read-only)
  - `RecipientEmail` (String, read-only)
  - `Subject` (String, editable, required, max 120)
  - `Body` (String (multiline), editable, required, max 2000)
  - `Decision` (Choice: Approve/Reject, required)
  - `ReviewerComments` (String multiline, optional)
- Validation rules:
  - If Decision=Approve → Subject and Body required
  - If Decision=Reject → ReviewerComments required
- SLA:
  - Due: 2 hours after creation
  - Warning: 1 hour
  - Escalation: email SME via Gmail connector (still using ninemush) **only if enabled**; otherwise no escalation.

Persistence:
- Store review outcome in Data Service entity `BirthdayGreetingReview` linked to `BirthdayGreetingLog`.

---

## 3. UiPath Activities and Packages Required

### 3.1 Packages (exact versions from validated registry)
- UiPath.System.Activities **26.2.3**
- UiPath.IntegrationService.Activities **1.24.0**
- UiPath.Act365.IntegrationService.Activities **4.0.5** (if required by specific connector actions)
- UiPath.GenAI.Activities **1.0.0**
- UiPath.Mail.Activities **2.7.11** (for local email utilities; primary send remains Integration Service)
- UiPath.DataService.Activities **25.9.3**
- UiPath.Persistence.Activities **1.8.1** (only if Action Center optional path enabled)
- UiPath.WebAPI.Activities **2.4.0** (only for internal service calls if needed; **no custom HTTP to Google**)
- Newtonsoft.Json **13.0.4**

### 3.2 Key activities (by function)
**Orchestrator / config**
- Get Asset
- Add Log Fields / Log Message
- Take Screenshot (on exception) + Upload to Storage Bucket (see below)

**Integration Service**
- Use Integration Service (connector-scoped activities)
- Gmail connector activities: Send Email (exact activity name depends on connector package binding)
- Google Calendar connector activities: Get Calendar / List Events (today)
- Google Contacts/People connector activities: Search Contacts / Get Contact details

**GenAI**
- GenAI: Generate Text (UiPath GenAI Activities)
- (Optional) GenAI: Evaluate/Moderate (if available in activities; otherwise implement self-check prompt + deterministic validations)

**Data Service**
- Create Record / Update Record / Get Records (for idempotency and audit)

**Storage Buckets**
- Upload Storage Object (run summary, error screenshot, sanitized prompt/response logs)

- **Connector**: Gmail (Integration Service)
- **Connection**: `ninemush@gmail.com`
- **Connection ID**: `0a0d5ee1-a1e8-477a-a943-58161e6f3272`
- **Used for**: sending birthday emails
- **Why connector vs custom SMTP/HTTP**: managed OAuth, reduced auth fragility, standard monitoring, and mandated by your platform rules.

### 4.2 Google Calendar (read Birthdays calendar)
- **Connector**: Google Calendar (Integration Service) — **to be provisioned**
- **Connection**: `GoogleCalendar_ninemush` (proposed)
- **Used for**: list today’s events from calendar named `""Birthdays""` using SME timezone date window.

### 4.3 Google Contacts/People (resolve recipient emails)
- **Connector**: Google Contacts / People (Integration Service) — **to be provisioned**
- **Connection**: `GoogleContactsPeople_ninemush` (proposed)
- **Used for**: search by full name, fetch email addresses and labels; apply `personal > home`.

### 4.4 UiPath GenAI Activities connection
- **Connector/Capability**: UiPath GenAI Activities
- **Existing connections**:
  - `prajwal.shambhu@uipath.com` (ID: `9d4f449a-0d3a-4755-9bba-1839fb337bcc`)
  - `prajwal.shambhu@uipath.com #2` (ID: `43afba75-1c5d-4a0f-b119-70736d0e90e0`)
- **Used for**: generating message body; guardrail self-check prompt.
- **Note**: This is “native UiPath capability” as required; **Azure OpenAI connection is explicitly not used**.

### 4.5 Data Service (entity operations)
- Entities defined in Section 9.
- Used for run audit, idempotency, and (optional) review records.

---

## 5. Exception Handling Strategy

### 5.1 Business exceptions (expected, non-failing)
Handled as “skips” with audit record creation:
- No birthdays today → end cleanly.
- No contact match → skip.
- Ambiguous contact match → skip.
- No email (neither personal nor home) → skip.
- Idempotency: already sent today → skip.
- Guardrail fail after retry → do not send; record status `GuardrailFail`.

### 5.2 System exceptions (failing)
Examples:
- Integration Service connector auth expired / revoked
- Google API throttling via connector
- Orchestrator transient failures
- GenAI service unavailable/timeouts

**Strategy**
- Use Try/Catch around each external call boundary (Calendar fetch, Contacts search, GenAI generation, Gmail send).
- Retries:
  - For transient connector errors: retry 2 times with exponential backoff (e.g., 5s, 15s).
  - For GenAI generation: 1 regeneration attempt with stricter prompt.
- If Calendar retrieval fails → **fail the job** (no partial work) because we cannot trust completeness.
- If a single person send fails → continue processing other events, but mark that item as `Error` and surface in logs.

### 5.3 Diagnostics and operability
Mandatory on every Catch:
- **Take Screenshot** (even if API-based, screenshot can capture minimal context; additionally store JSON context)
- Write structured log with:
  - `RunDate`, `EventId`, `FullName`, `Stage`, `ExceptionType`, `Message`, `CorrelationId`
- Upload to Storage Bucket:
  - `error.png`
  - `context.json` (sanitized)
  - `stacktrace.txt`

### 5.4 Dead-letter handling
Not using Orchestrator Queues; therefore “dead-letter” is implemented as:
- Data Service record status = `Error` with `ErrorStage` and `ErrorDetails`
- Next day run is independent; manual re-run can be initiated from Orchestrator with same date window (idempotency prevents duplicates).

---

## 6. Security Considerations

### 6.1 Credential and secret management
- All OAuth tokens are handled by **Integration Service connections**; no passwords stored in workflows.
- Config values stored in **Orchestrator Assets** (non-secret unless needed).

### 6.2 RBAC and least privilege
- Orchestrator folder permissions:
  - Robots: execute only
  - Developers: edit packages, assets (limited)
  - SME: view logs, view job status (optional)
- Integration Service connections restricted to this folder.

### 6.3 Data protection
- Data Service stores only necessary metadata:
  - recipient email, name, send status, timestamps
  - avoid storing full GenAI prompt/response unless explicitly enabled (`StorePromptArtifacts` asset).
- Storage Bucket artifacts are sanitized; no secrets/tokens ever written.

### 6.4 Audit trail
- Orchestrator job logs + Data Service audit entity provide traceability of every send/skip decision.

---

## 7. Test Strategy (Test Manager)

### 7.1 Automated tests
Create a dedicated **Test Project** and register in **Test Manager**:
- Unit tests (workflow-level with mocked inputs):
  - Name parsing → first name extraction
  - Email selection rule (personal > home)
  - Ambiguous match handling
  - Guardrail validation logic (length, forbidden phrases)
  - Subject template correctness
- Integration tests (sandbox / controlled data):
  - Google Calendar returns known events for a test date
  - Google Contacts lookup returns known emails/labels
  - Gmail send to a test recipient mailbox (or SME’s own) with “dry-run mode” asset enabled

### 7.2 UAT approach
- Run for a controlled week using a test “Birthdays” calendar and test contacts.
- Then switch calendar asset to production `""Birthdays""`.

### 7.3 Regression suite
- Daily scheduled job is low risk; regression suite run on:
  - connector updates
  - prompt/guardrail changes
  - platform upgrades

---

## 7a. Governance Compliance
Automation Ops is not available; therefore:
- We implement internal governance via:
  - strict naming conventions (assets, processes, entities)
  - mandatory Try/Catch around all connector calls
  - mandatory screenshot + artifact upload on exceptions
  - secrets only via Integration Service connections

---

## 8. Data Model and Entity Design (Data Service)

### 8.1 Entity: `BirthdayGreetingLog`
Purpose: audit + idempotency + operational reporting.

Fields:
- `RunDate` (Date) — required, indexed
- `EventId` (String) — from calendar event, optional
- `CalendarName` (String) — default “Birthdays”
- `FullName` (String) — required
- `FirstName` (String) — optional
- `ContactResolutionStatus` (Choice: `UniqueMatch`, `NoMatch`, `AmbiguousMatch`) — required
- `RecipientEmail` (String) — optional
- `RecipientEmailLabel` (Choice: `personal`, `home`, `none`) — required
- `MessageSubject` (String) — optional
- `MessageBodyHash` (String) — optional (hash for troubleshooting without storing body)
- `SendStatus` (Choice: `Sent`, `Skipped`, `GuardrailFail`, `Error`) — required
- `SkipReason` (Choice: `NoBirthdays`, `NoMatch`, `AmbiguousMatch`, `NoEmail`, `AlreadySent`, `GuardrailFail`) — optional
- `SentAt` (DateTime) — optional
- `OrchestratorJobId` (String) — required
- `ErrorStage` (String) — optional
- `ErrorDetails` (String) — optional (sanitized)
- `StorageBucketPath` (String) — optional (link to run artifacts)

Idempotency rule:
- Consider “already sent” if `RunDate = today` AND (`RecipientEmail = X` OR (`FullName = Y` AND `SendStatus = Sent`)).

### 8.2 Optional Entity: `BirthdayGreetingReview` (only if Action Center enabled)
Fields:
- `GreetingLogId` (Relation to `BirthdayGreetingLog`) — required
- `TaskId` (String) — required
- `Decision` (Choice: Approve/Reject) — required
- `ApprovedSubject` (String) — optional
- `ApprovedBody` (String) — optional
- `ReviewerComments` (String) — optional
- `ReviewedAt` (DateTime) — optional

---

## 8. Agent Architecture

> Note: Because Agents availability is detected with limited certainty, the **core solution does not depend on Agents**. This section defines an **optional** Agent that can be enabled once verified.

### 8.1 Agent Type
- **Autonomous agent** (optional enhancement)

### 8.2 Agent Identity
- **Name**: `BirthdayMessageAgent`
- **Purpose**: Generate a short birthday email body in SME’s voice (warm, funny, sarcastic) while adhering to guardrails.
- **Behavioral system prompt (high level)**:
  - “Write a brief, email-appropriate birthday greeting in a warm, funny, sarcastic tone. Do not invent facts, do not mention relationship, do not request money, do not include sensitive topics, keep it concise.”

--- PDD CONTENT (input to LLM) ---
"## 1. Executive Summary
This Process Design Document (PDD) defines the automation of a daily “birthday greetings” process that currently relies on a manual 8:00 AM check of a dedicated Google Calendar (“Birthdays”) followed by composing and sending a personal email from the SME’s Gmail account. The SME’s goal is to eliminate missed greetings by running a fully autonomous unattended workflow each morning at 8:00 AM in the SME’s timezone. The future-state automation will retrieve today’s birthday events from the “Birthdays” Google Calendar, look up the corresponding contact in Google Contacts/People to obtain a recipient email address (preferring “personal” over “home” when multiple are present), generate a short warm/funny/sarcastic message in the SME’s voice using UiPath native GenAI capabilities (not OpenAI), and send the email via the Gmail Integration Service connector using the connection **ninemush@gmail.com**. If no email is found for a contact, the automation will take no action (silent skip), as confirmed by the SME.

## 2. Process Scope
The scope of this automation includes a single daily unattended run initiated by an Orchestrator schedule trigger at 8:00 AM in the SME’s timezone. The process begins by retrieving birthday events for “today” from the Google Calendar named “Birthdays,” then iterating through each birthday event and resolving the recipient’s email address from Google Contacts/People. If an email is found, the process generates and sends a personalized birthday email from **ninemush@gmail.com** via Integration Service’s Gmail connector. The content must be AI-generated but sound like the SME: warm, funny, and sarcastic, while remaining appropriate for email.  

Out of scope for this iteration are photo selection and inclusion from Google Photos, any use of Google Drive, any use of external OpenAI/Azure OpenAI connectors, and any notifications via Slack, Microsoft Teams, or Twilio. Human review is not required for normal operation because the SME requested a fully autonomous solution; however, message guardrails and basic validation are in scope to reduce risk of inappropriate or overly sensitive content.

## 3. As-Is Process Description

![As-Is Process Map](/api/ideas/c2cf6199-5cb2-4f07-a536-5791719bbae3/process-map/image?viewType=as-is&v=1774615443210)
The current process is performed manually by the SME each day and follows the approved As‑Is process map. The process starts at 8:00 AM (Step “8:00 AM Daily Birthday Check Starts”). The SME opens Google Calendar (Step “Open Google Calendar”), selects the dedicated “Birthdays” calendar (Step “Select ‘Birthdays’ Calendar”), and checks the current day for birthday events (Step “Check Today for Birthday Events”). A decision is made on whether any birthdays exist today (Step “Any Birthdays Today?”). If none exist, the process ends (Step “End (No Birthdays)”).  

If birthdays exist, the SME processes each birthday event: the person’s name is identified from the event (Step “For Each Birthday Event, Identify Person Name”), and the SME looks up the person in Google Contacts (Step “Look Up Contact in Google Contacts”). A decision is made as to whether an email address is available (Step “Email Address Found?”). If an email is found, the SME selects the preferred email when multiple are present (Step “Choose Preferred Email (Personal if Multiple)”), drafts a personal birthday message in their own voice (Step “Draft Personal Birthday Message (Your Voice)”), and sends the email via Gmail (Step “Send Email from Gmail”), ending for that event (Step “Birthday Greeting Sent End”). If no email is found, the SME silently skips sending (Step “Skip Sending (No Email Found)” as corrected to a silent skip) and proceeds to the next event. The SME repeats until no birthday events remain (Step “More Birthday Events Remaining?” leading to “End (All Birthdays Processed)”).

## 4. To-Be Process Description

![To-Be Process Map](/api/ideas/c2cf6199-5cb2-4f07-a536-5791719bbae3/process-map/image?viewType=to-be&v=1774615443210)
In the automated future state, the workflow executes unattended at 8:00 AM in the SME’s timezone (To‑Be Step 1.0 “8:00 AM Daily Trigger (Your Timezone)”) using UiPath Orchestrator Triggers. The automation retrieves today’s birthday events from the Google Calendar named “Birthdays” (To‑Be Step 2.0 “Retrieve Today’s Birthday Events from ‘Birthdays’ Calendar”) through UiPath Integration Service (Google Calendar connector connection to be added).  

The workflow determines whether any birthdays occur today (To‑Be Step 3.0 “Any Birthdays Today?”). If no birthdays are found, the process ends immediately without further action (To‑Be Step 4.0 “End (No Birthdays Today)”). If birthdays exist, the workflow iterates over each birthday event (To‑Be Step 4.1 “For Each Birthday Event”). For each event, it parses the full name from the calendar event (To‑Be Step 5.0 “Parse Full Name from Calendar Event”).  

Next, the automation searches Google Contacts/People for a matching contact by name (To‑Be Step 6.0 “Find Matching Contact(s) by Name”) via Integration Service (Google Contacts/People connection to be added). A decision step evaluates whether a unique match is found (To‑Be Step 7.0 “Unique Contact Match Found?”). If the match is ambiguous or no match is found, the workflow silently skips that person (To‑Be Step 7.1 “Silently Skip (Ambiguous/No Match)”) and continues with the next birthday event.  

When a unique contact match is found, the automation extracts email addresses labeled “home” and “personal” (To‑Be Step 8.0 “Extract Email Addresses (Home/Personal)”) and determines whether any email exists (To‑Be Step 9.0 “Any Email Found?”). If no email is present, it silently skips with no outbound notification (To‑Be Step 9.1 “Silently Skip (No Email on Contact)”), as explicitly confirmed by the SME. If an email is available, the workflow selects the recipient email using the rule “personal > home” (To‑Be Step 10.0 “Select Recipient Email (Personal > Home)”).  

The automation then composes the prompt inputs needed to produce a message in the SME’s voice (To‑Be Step 11.0 “Compose Prompt Inputs”), including at minimum the person’s first name derived from the full name. Using UiPath native capabilities (not OpenAI), the process generates the birthday email body in the SME’s warm, funny, sarcastic style (To‑Be Step 12.0 “Generate Birthday Email Body (Your Voice)”) with UiPath GenAI Activities (and, if enabled/validated on the tenant, UiPath Agents as the message-generation “agent”). The generated message is checked against guardrails (To‑Be Step 13.0 “Message Meets Guardrails? (tone, length, no sensitive claims)”) to ensure it stays appropriate and safe. When guardrails pass, the automation sends the email via Integration Service’s Gmail connector using the connection **ninemush@gmail.com** (To‑Be Step 14.0 “Send Email via Gmail”). The subject line format selected by the SME is: **“Happy Birthday, {FirstName}!”**. The workflow then continues to the next birthday event until all are processed (To‑Be Step “More Birthday Events Remaining?” leading to “End (All Birthdays Processed)”).

## 5. Pain Points and Inefficiencies
The current process depends entirely on the SME remembering to perform a manual daily check at 8:00 AM. The primary pain point is reliability: the SME sometimes forgets, resulting in missed greetings and a poor experience for recipients. The process is also repetitive and time-consuming when multiple birthdays occur on the same day, requiring repeated context switching between Google Calendar, Google Contacts, and Gmail. Additionally, manual message creation introduces variability in tone and length depending on time constraints and attention, and manual contact lookup increases the chance of errors when contacts have multiple email addresses or when names are similar.

## 6. Automation Opportunity Assessment
This is a strong candidate for unattended automation because it is time-triggered, structured, and relies on digital systems with available integration points. The optimal automation type is **Hybrid (Workflow + GenAI)**: deterministic orchestration for date-based retrieval, contact lookup, and email sending; and generative text creation for producing a “your voice” message. UiPath Orchestrator Triggers provide reliable daily execution at 8:00 AM in the SME’s timezone. Integration Service provides the required system APIs for Gmail immediately (already connected as **ninemush@gmail.com**) and can be extended by adding Google Calendar and Google Contacts/People connections. UiPath GenAI Activities enable native generation without using OpenAI/Azure OpenAI connectors, meeting the SME’s constraint.  

Expected benefits include near-elimination of missed birthday emails, consistent “voice” adherence, reduced manual effort, and improved scalability when multiple birthdays occur in one day. The process is also low-risk operationally because the “no email found” condition results in a silent skip, avoiding accidental mis-sends.

## 7. Assumptions and Exceptions
This design assumes that the Google Calendar named “Birthdays” contains an event for each person’s birthday on the correct date and that the event title (or a consistently readable field) includes the person’s full name in a parseable format. It assumes the SME’s contacts are present in Google Contacts/People under a matching name and that emails are labeled as “personal” and/or “home” to support the preference rule. It also assumes that Integration Service connections for Google Calendar and Google Contacts/People can be added and authorized on the tenant.  

Key exceptions and how the To‑Be handles them are as follows. When there are no birthdays today, the workflow ends with no notifications and no “forgot” scenario. When a contact match is ambiguous (multiple matches for the same name) or not found, the workflow silently skips that birthday event. When a contact exists but has no email addresses labeled home or personal (or no email at all), the workflow silently skips and performs no outbound notification, per SME confirmation. When multiple emails exist, the automation selects the personal email; if personal is not available but home is, it uses home.  

Finally, the solution assumes the process runs unattended with no user interaction. If any connector authentication expires or the Google connections are not authorized, the job will fail and require operational remediation (credential/connection refresh).

## 8. Data and System Requirements
The automation requires the following systems and data elements. Google Calendar access is required to read the “Birthdays” calendar and retrieve events for “today” based on the SME’s timezone. Data required from calendar events includes at minimum the event date and the person’s full name (as represented in the event title/summary). Google Contacts/People access is required to search contacts by name and retrieve email addresses and their labels; the automation uses these labels to choose the recipient with the rule “personal > home.” Gmail access is required to send emails from the SME’s mailbox via UiPath Integration Service using the existing connector connection **ninemush@gmail.com**.  

Within UiPath, Orchestrator is required for scheduling (Triggers), execution on unattended robots (11 available), and operational logging. UiPath GenAI Activities are required to generate the email body in the SME’s voice using native UiPath capabilities, explicitly excluding OpenAI/Azure OpenAI connectors. The process should store configurable values (e.g., timezone, calendar name “Birthdays,” subject template “Happy Birthday, {FirstName}!”, tone/style instructions) as Orchestrator Assets to avoid code changes when refining “voice.”  

No use of Google Drive is permitted for this iteration, and no integration with Slack/Teams/Twilio is required. Photos from Google Photos are explicitly deferred to a future iteration and are not included in this PDD’s system requirements."

## 4. Process Context (from Pipeline)

### Idea Description

Automate birthday greetings to friends and family

### PDD Summary

## 1. Executive Summary
This Process Design Document (PDD) defines the automation of a daily “birthday greetings” process that currently relies on a manual 8:00 AM check of a dedicated Google Calendar (“Birthdays”) followed by composing and sending a personal email from the SME’s Gmail account. The SME’s goal is to eliminate missed greetings by running a fully autonomous unattended workflow each morning at 8:00 AM in the SME’s timezone. The future-state automation will retrieve today’s birthday events from the “Birthdays” Google Calendar, look up the corresponding contact in Google Contacts/People to obtain a recipient email address (preferring “personal” over “home” when multiple are present), generate a short warm/funny/sarcastic message in the SME’s voice using UiPath native GenAI capabilities (not OpenAI), and send the email via the Gmail Integration Service connector using the connection **ninemush@gmail.com**. If no email is found for a contact, the automation will take no action (silent skip), as confirmed by the SME.

## 2. Process Scope
The scope of this automation includes a single daily unattended run initiated by an Orchestrator schedule trigger at 8:00 AM in the SME’s timezone. The process begins by retrieving birthday events for “today” from the Google Calendar named “Birthdays,” then iterating through each birthday event and resolving the recipient’s email address from Google Contacts/People. If an email is found, the process generates and sends a personalized birthday email from **ninemush@gmail.com** via Integration Service’s Gmail connector. The content must be AI-generated but sound like the SME: warm, funny, and sarcastic, while remaining appropriate for email.  

Out of scope for this iteration are photo selection and inclusion from Google Photos, any use of Google Drive, any use of external OpenAI/Azure OpenAI connectors, and any notifications via Slack, Microsoft Teams, or Twilio. Human review is not required for normal operation because the S...

### SDD Summary

## 1. Automation Architecture Overview

### 1.1 Chosen automation type and rationale
This process is best delivered as **Hybrid (Deterministic RPA workflow + Native GenAI)**:
- **RPA (unattended)** is ideal for the deterministic steps: schedule at 8:00 AM in SME timezone, read Google Calendar events, look up Google Contacts emails, apply the “personal > home” rule, and send mail via Gmail connector. This must be **fully autonomous** and repeatable.
- **GenAI (UiPath-native)** is ideal for the non-deterministic step: generating a short message that matches the SME’s warm/funny/sarcastic voice with guardrails.

**We are not using a pure Agent-only design** because:
- Most steps are deterministic and have clear integration connectors; a workflow is more controllable, testable, and cheaper to operate.
- The tenant indicates **Agents availability with limited confidence**. We will use **GenAI Activities** as the primary message generator and treat “Agents” as an optional enhancement (see Section 8) without making the core solution depend on uncertain platform reachability.

**We are not using attended automation** because:
- Only unattended slots are available (11) and the SME requires fully autonomous execution.

### 1.2 Orchestration pattern
**Single-process scheduled unattended automation** (not dispatcher/performer, not queue fan-out) is optimal because:
- Daily volume is small (typically a handful of birthdays).
- There is no multi-transaction SLA requiring parallelism.
- A queue-driven model would add operational overhead (queues, retries, reconciliation) without meaningful benefit.

If volume grows materially (e.g., dozens+ per day across multiple calendars), we can evolve to **Dispatcher/Performer with Orchestrator Queues** for fan-out and parallel sends, but it is intentionally not the first design.

### 1.3 UiPath services used (and why)
- **Orchestrator**: schedule trigger at 08:00 SME timezone; process deployment; assets; logs; alerts (via job failures); robo...

**Automation Type:** hybrid
**Rationale:** Calendar/event retrieval and email sending are deterministic (RPA), but generating a “warm/funny/sarcastic” message in your personal voice requires generative reasoning with safety checks (agent), making a hybrid the most maintainable design.
**Feasibility Complexity:** medium
**Effort Estimate:** 3-5 days

## 5. Business Process Overview

### Process Steps

| # | Step | Role | System | Type | Pain Point |
|---|------|------|--------|------|------------|
| 1 | 8:00 AM Daily Trigger (Your Timezone) | System | Orchestrator Triggers | start | — |
| 2 | Retrieve Today's Birthday Events from ""Birthdays"" Calendar | System | Integration Service - Google Calendar (connection to be added) | task | — |
| 3 | Any Birthdays Today? | System | Workflow | decision | — |
| 4 | End (No Birthdays Today) | System | Orchestrator | end | — |
| 5 | For Each Birthday Event | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 6 | Parse Full Name from Calendar Event | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 7 | Find Matching Contact(s) by Name | System | Integration Service - Google Contacts/People (connection to be added) | task | — |
| 8 | Unique Contact Match Found? | System | Workflow | decision | — |
| 9 | Extract Email Addresses (Home/Personal) | System | Integration Service - Google Contacts/People (connection to be added) | task | — |
| 10 | Silently Skip (Ambiguous/No Match) | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 11 | Any Email Found? | System | Workflow | decision | — |
| 12 | Select Recipient Email (Personal > Home) | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 13 | Silently Skip (No Email on Contact) | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 14 | Compose Prompt Inputs (FirstName, optional short context) | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 15 | Generate Birthday Email Body (Your Voice) | Birthday Message Agent | UiPath Agents + UiPath GenAI Activities | agent-task | — |
| 16 | Message Meets Guardrails? (tone, length, no sensitive claims) | Birthday Message Agent | UiPath Agents | agent-decision | — |
| 17 | Send Email via Gmail | System | Integration Service - Gmail (connection: ninemush@gmail.com) | task | — |
| 18 | Route to Action Center for Review | System | Action Center | task | — |
| 19 | Human Review Decision | You | Action Center | decision | — |
| 20 | Send Approved Email via Gmail | System | Integration Service - Gmail (connection: ninemush@gmail.com) | task | — |
| 21 | Skip Sending (Rejected/Timed Out) | System | Workflow | task | — |
| 22 | More Birthday Events Remaining? | System | Workflow | decision | — |

### User Roles Involved

- Birthday Message Agent
- You

### Decision Points (Process Map Topology)

**Any Birthdays Today?**
  - [No] → End (No Birthdays Today)

**Unique Contact Match Found?**
  - [Yes] → Extract Email Addresses (Home/Personal)
  - [No] → Silently Skip (Ambiguous/No Match)

**Any Email Found?**
  - [Yes] → Select Recipient Email (Personal > Home)
  - [No] → Silently Skip (No Email on Contact)

**Human Review Decision**
  - [Approved] → Send Approved Email via Gmail
  - [Rejected/Timeout] → Skip Sending (Rejected/Timed Out)

**More Birthday Events Remaining?**
  - [→] → End (No Birthdays Today)

## 11. Trigger Configuration

Based on the process analysis, the following trigger configuration is recommended:

| # | Trigger Type | Reason | Configuration |
|---|-------------|--------|---------------|
| 1 | **Schedule** | Defined in SDD orchestrator_artifacts: BDAY_0800_Dispatcher_TimeTrigger | SDD-specified: BDAY_0800_Dispatcher_TimeTrigger | Cron: 0 0 8 ? * * * | Daily 8:00 AM (SME timezone enforced in Orchestrator trigger configuration) to run dispatcher logic that loads today’s birthdays. |
| 2 | **Queue** | Defined in SDD orchestrator_artifacts: BDAY_Performer_QueueTrigger | SDD-specified: BDAY_Performer_QueueTrigger | Queue: BDAY_GREETINGS_SEND | Starts performer when new items arrive to generate guarded message and send greeting email. |
